 BY ORDER OF THE  SECRETARY OF THE AIR FORCE AIR FORCE INSTRUCTION 11-2EC-130J VOLUME 3 8 APRIL 2015 Flying Operations  COMPLIANCE WITH THIS PUBLICATION IS MANDATORY EC-130J—OPERATIONS PROCEDURES ACCESSIBILITY:  Publications and forms are available on the e-Publishing website at www.epublishing.af.mil for downloading or ordering. RELEASABILITY:  There are no releasability restrictions on this publication.  OPR:   HQ AFSOC/A3V  Supersedes:   AFI11-2EC-130JV3, 21 January 2010 Certified by: AF/A3O (Brig Gen Giovanni K. Tuck) Pages: 293   instruction implements  Air  Force  Instruction  (AFI)  11-200,  Aircrew  Training, This Standardization/Evaluation, and General Operations Structure, and AFI 11-202, Vol 3, General Flight  Rules.    It  applies  to  all  EC130J  units,  and  it  provides  the  most  acceptable  policies  and procedures  for  most  circumstances,  but  does  not  replace  sound  judgment.    This  instruction applies to the Air National Guard (ANG).  This publication does not apply to Air Force Reserve Command (AFRC) units.  Subordinate units may supplement this instruction in accordance with (IAW)  Paragraph  1.5.    This  publication  requires  the  collection  and  or  maintenance  of information  protected  by  the  Privacy  Act  of  1974  authorized  by  Air  Force  Policy  Directive (AFPD)  11-2,  Aircrew  Operations.    When  personal  information  is  collected,  personnel  will  be provided with a Privacy Act Statement.  The applicable Privacy Act System of Records Notice (SORN),  F011  AF  XO  A,  is  available  at  http://privacy.defense.gov/notices/usaf/.    The authority for maintenance of the Automated Records Management System (ARMS) is 37 U.S.C. 301a  (Incentive  Pay),  Public  Law  92-204,  Section  715  (Appropriations  Act  for  1973),  Public Laws  93-570  (Appropriation  Act  for  1974),  93-294  (Aviation  Career  Incentive  Act  of  1974), DoD  Directive  7730.57  (Aviation  Career  Incentive  Act  of  1974  and  Required  Annual  Report, February 5, 1976, with Changes 1 and 2); and E.O. 9397 (SSN) as amended by Executive Order 13478, Amendments to Executive Order 9397 Relating to Federal Agency Use of Social Security Numbers,  November  18,  2008.    Refer  recommended  changes  and  questions  about  this publication to the Office of Primary Responsibility (OPR) using the Air Force (AF) Form 847, Recommendation  for  Change  of  Publication;  route  AF  Form  847s  from  the  field  through  the appropriate functional’s chain of command.  Unless prescribed within this publication, requests for  waivers  must  be  submitted  through  chain  of  command  to  the  OPR  listed  above  for consideration and approval.  Ensure that all records created as a result of processes prescribed in   2  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 this  publication  are  maintained  in  accordance  with  Air  Force  Manual  (AFMAN)  33-363, Management of Records, and disposed of in accordance with the Air Force Records Disposition Schedule (RDS) located in the Air Force Records Information Management System (AFRIMS). SUMMARY OF CHANGES This  publication  has  been  substantially  revised  and  aligned  with  the  MC-130J  regulation  and must  be  completely  reviewed.    Reference  to  Commando  Solo  operations  has  been  moved  to Attachment 5.  Chapter 17 encompasses a majority of the tactical employment guidance.  Night Vision  Goggle  (NVG)  operations  no  longer  reside  in  one  chapter  and  are  instead  integrated within the appropriate sections.  Tier requirements have been annotated. Rescue Lanyard.   .....................................................................................................  248 Attachment 1—GLOSSARY OF REFERENCES AND SUPPORTING INFORMATION   Attachment 2—INFILTRATION/EXFILTRATION PROCEDURES   Attachment 3—COMBAT OFFLOAD PROCEDURES      249 276 283 Attachment 4—ELECTRONIC COMMUNICATIONS SYSTEMS OPERATOR DUTIES     285 Attachment 5—COMMANDO SOLO OPERATIONS     289   12  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 Chapter 1 GENRAL INFORMATION 1.1.  General.  This  AFI  provides  operational  guidelines  and  restrictions  for  EC-130J Commando Solo  (CS) and Super J (SJ) operations.   It  is  a  compilation  of information  from  all aircraft  flight  manuals,  Flight  Information  Publications  (FLIP)  and  other  Air  Force  directives, and is an original source document for many areas.  Basic source directives have precedence in the case of any conflicts, revisions, and matters of interpretation.  For those areas where this AFI is the source document, waiver authority will be in accordance with applicable paragraph.  For those  areas  where  this  AFI  repeats  information  contained  in  other  source  documents,  waiver authority  will  be  in  accordance  with  those  source  documents.    This  instruction  is  regulatory  in nature  and  takes  precedence  over  guidance  in  Air  Force  Tactics,  Techniques,  and  Procedures (AFTTP).  HQ AFSOC Standardization/Evaluation (HQ AFSOC/A3V) has overall responsibility for the administration of this volume.  The NGB is considered a Major Command (MAJCOM) for the purpose of this AFI. 1.2.  Applicability. 1.2.1.  This  AFI  is  applicable to all individuals/units operating EC-130J (Commando Solo), EC130J  (Super  J),  as  well  as  other  EC-130J  variants,  and  backup  aircraft  inventory  (BAI) C130J operated by the flying unit. 1.2.2.  This AFI will be used by all agencies involved in or supporting EC-130J (Commando Solo  and  Super J)  operations.    Copies  will  be  current  and  available  to  planning  staffs  from headquarters to aircrew level.  (T-2) 1.3.  Key Definitions: 1.3.1.  “Will” and “Shall” indicate a mandatory requirement. 1.3.2.  “Should” indicates a preferred, but not mandatory, method of accomplishment. 1.3.3.  “May” indicates an acceptable or suggested means of accomplishment. 1.3.4.  “WARNING”  indicates  operating  procedures,  techniques,  etc.,  which  may  result  in personal injury or loss of life if not carefully followed. 1.3.5.  “CAUTION”  indicates  operating  procedures,  techniques,  etc.,  which  may  result  in damage to equipment if not carefully followed. 1.3.6.  “Note” indicates operating procedures, techniques, etc., which are considered essential to emphasize. 1.3.7.  See Attachment 1, Glossary of References and Supporting Information, for additional terms. 1.4.  Deviations and Waivers.  Do not deviate from the policies and guidance in this AFI except when  the  situation  demands  immediate  action  to  ensure  safety.    Although  this  publication provides  guidance  for  aircraft  operations  under  most  circumstances,  it  is  not  a  substitute  for sound  judgment.    When  it  is  necessary  to  protect  the  crew  and  aircraft  from  a  situation  not covered by this instruction and when immediate action is required, the Pilot in Command (PIC) has ultimate authority and responsibility for the course of action to be taken.  Report deviations, AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   13  without  waiver,  through  channels  to  HQ  AFSOC/A3  within  48  hours,  followed  by  a  written report,  if  requested.    Unless  otherwise  indicated,  HQ  AFSOC/A3  is  the  waiver  authority  for operational  procedure  requirements  contained  in  this  volume.    Request  waivers  through Standardization/Evaluation (Stan/Eval) and MAJCOM channels.  (T-2) 1.4.1.  Tier requirements refer to waiver authority based on level of risk. 1.4.1.1.  “Tier 0”  (T-0) requirements are reserved for requirements that non-compliance is determined and waived by respective non-Air Force authority. 1.4.1.2.  “Tier 1”  (T-1) requirements are reserved for requirements that non-compliance may  put  airman,  mission,  or  program  strongly  at  risk,  and  may  only  be  waived  by  the MAJCOM/CC  or  delegate  with  concurrence  of  publication  approver.    When  multiple MAJCOMs are affected, then T-1 is appropriate. 1.4.1.2.1.  HQ AFFSA/XOF will initiate Tier 1 waivers.  Following a MAJCOM/CC (delegable no lower than MAJCOM/A3) request, HQ AFFSA/XOF will request AFI Certifying  Official  approval.    Tier  1  waiver  renewal  requests  will  only  be  accepted from MAJCOM Stan/Eval and approved by the HQ AFFSA/CC. 1.4.1.3.  “Tier  2”    (T-2)  requirements  are  reserved  for  requirements  that  potentially  put the  mission  at  risk  or  potentially  degrade  the  mission  or  program,  and  may  only  be waived by the MAJCOM/CC or delegate. 1.4.1.4.  “Tier 3”  (T-3) requirements are reserved for requirements that non-compliance has  a  remote  risk  of  mission  failure,  and  may  be  waived  by  the  Wing/CC  but  no  lower than the OG/CC. 1.4.2.  AFSOC/A3 may delegate this authority to Commander Special Operations Air Forces (COMAFSOF) for operationally assigned SOF forces during contingency operations.  If HQ AFSOC/A3 chooses to delegate waiver authority, it will be done in writing and will specify which portions of this instruction may be waived by the COMAFSOF. 1.4.2.1.  When waiver authority is delegated, HQ AFSOC/A3V will receive a copy of all approved waivers. 1.5.  Supplements.  MAJCOM may supplement  this volume according to  AFI 11-200, Aircrew Training,  Standardization/Evaluation,  and  General  Operations  Structure.    These  supplements will  not  duplicate  or  be  less  restrictive  than  the  provisions  of  this  instruction.    Forward MAJCOM  supplements  to  HQ  AFSOC/A3V  and  Air  Force  Flight  Standards  Agency (AFFSA)/XOF  for  approval  before  publication  and  provide  HQ  AFFSA/XOF  one  copy  after publication.  File supplements according to AFI  33-360, Publications and Forms Management.  (T-2) 1.5.1.  Local Operating Procedures.  IAW Chapter 10 of this instruction. 1.6.  Requisitioning Procedures.  Order this AFI through the servicing Publications Distribution Office.    Unit  commanders  provide  copies  for  all  aircrew  members  and  associated  support personnel.  This publication is available digitally on www.epublishing.af.mil. 1.7.  Distribution.  This  instruction  is  published  as  one  complete  document  and  distributed  as such.  Unit commanders will assure distribution of this instruction to all crew members.  (T-3) 1.8.  Roles and Responsibilities.  Refer to Chapter 2 for roles and responsibilities.   14  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 Chapter 2 COMMAND AND CONTROL (C2) 2.1.  General.  The AFSOC C2 system is based on the principles of centralized monitoring and decentralized  control  and  execution.    The  result  is  a  C2  mechanism  which  keeps  the  AFSOC Commander (CC) informed of the  current  status  of AFSOC forces while enabling the Wing or Group Commander to exercise control over day-to-day operations.  This chapter contains Tier 1 requirements in the administrative control and state active duty sections; Tier 2 requirements in general,  operational  control,  waiver  and  approval  authority,  administrative  control,  mission monitoring,  designation  of  COMASOF,    mission  commander,  pilot  in  command,  airborne mission commander, deputy mission commander, and mission clearance decision sections.  (T2) 2.2.  Operational  Control  (OPCON).  IAW  USSOCOM  Directive  10-1,  COMAFSOC exercises command authority consistent with assignment of OPCON over all active and reserve Air  Force  SOF  stationed  in  the  CONUS,  to  include  Air  National  Guard  (Training  Oversight (TOS)  only  IAW  JP  1).    OCONUS  forces  are  apportioned  OPCON  IAW  the  Global  Force Management Implementation Guidance (GFMIG), normally to the CCDR of the theater in which they  reside.    The  CCDR  will  normally  delegate  OPCON  to  the  Theater  Special  Operations Command  (TSOC)  for  that  theater.    In  practice,  responsibility  for  planning  and  executing AFSOC missions is routinely delegated to the Wing or Group Commander.  The Wing or Group Commander,  in  turn,  exercises  control  of  non-close-hold  missions  through  the  command  post supporting the wing or group.  In the event that assigned forces undergo a Change in Operational Control (CHOP), responsibility for mission monitoring passes from the wing or group C2 facility to the gaining command.  Changeover will be accomplished IAW the pertinent Operational Plan, Operational  Order, or deployment or execution order.  When ANG aircrews operate in a status other than Title 10, the members’ state governor, typically through delineated authorities to their appointed  Adjutant  General  (TAG),  will  control  aircrews  when  executing  Continental  United States  (CONUS)  Domestic  Operations  (DOMOP)  missions.    The  ANG  Command  Center  may serve as the reporting agency for ANG aircraft supporting ANG missions.  (T-2) 2.3.  Waiver and Approval Authorities.  (T-2) 2.3.1.  Wg/CCs or equivalent hold waiver/approval authority for items normally authorized at or below wing level when their forces are employed in: 2.3.1.1.  Deployments. 2.3.1.2.  Air Apportionment Allocation Conference taskings. 2.3.1.3.  Joint Air Apportionment Allocation Conference (JAAAC) taskings. 2.3.1.4.  Joint  Combined  Exchange  Training  (JCET)/Counter  Narcotics  Training missions. 2.3.1.5.  Other  specified  missions  as  tasked  via  the  SOF  Air  Tasking  Order  (ATO)  in SOF applications. 2.3.1.6.  CONUS  and  Outside  CONUS  (OCONUS)  forces  depart  a  TSOC/Joint  Special Operations  Air  Component  (JSOAC)  Area  of  Responsibility  (AOR)  enroute  to  United States Northern Command (NORTHCOM) AOR. AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   15  2.3.1.7.  Air Reserve Component (ARC) forces (under Title 10). 2.3.1.8.  Depart  home  station  for  AFSOC-directed  contingencies/deployments/exercises (under Title 10). 2.3.2.  Operational waivers will be coordinated through Stan/Eval channels.  Waiver requests will  normally  be  the  responsibility  of  the  C2  agency  with  the  operational  control  of  the mission. 2.3.3.  Wg/CC  OPCON  terminates  when  forces  enter  a  TSOC/JSOAC  AOR  and  picks  up when forces exit a TSOC/JSOAC AOR. 2.4.  ANG Forces OPCON/Administrative Control (ADCON). 2.4.1.  OPCON (Title 10).  When 193rd SOW forces are mobilized,  AFSOC will normally exercise  command  authority  consistent  with  assignment  of  OPCON  over  those  forces  until they are transferred with a specified command relationship of OPCON (CHOPed) to another Combatant  Command.  Deploying ANG members will be assigned to  201 Mission Support Squadron,  Air  National  Guard  Readiness  Center  (ANGRC),  Andrews  AFB,  MD  for ADCON, while COMAFSOC will retain specified ADCON IAW with the Memorandum of Agreement  between  the  Commonwealth  of  Pennsylvania,  the  National  Guard  Bureau,  and AFSOC.  COMAFSOC will transfer specified ADCON authorities to the Commander of Air Force  Forces  (COMAFFOR)  of  the  gaining  CCMD  IAW  established  Memoranda  of Agreement.  (T-1) 2.4.2.  Control  under  USC  Title  32.    The  Commonwealth  of  Pennsylvania  (PA)  Governor controls PA ANG forces, typically through the appointed TAG, when executing missions in Title 32 status.  PA ANG Title 32 status extends to those members who are in PA Excepted State  Technician  status  and  Inactive  Duty  Status  (Rescheduled)  Unit  Training  Assemblies (UTA) or Additional Flight Training Periods (AFTP).  Authority over forces made available to  another  state  may  be  transferred  to  that  state’s  governor  IAW  agreements  between  the states.  PA ANG members operating in Title 32 status are subject to the PA Code of Military Justice (PCMJ).  Members may be gained into Title 10 status at any time. 2.5.  Mission  Monitoring.  The  AFSOC  Operations  Center  monitors  all  off-station  AFSOC aircraft  via  Theater  Battle  Management  Core  Systems  (TBMCS)  –  Execution  Status  and Monitoring (ESTAT), the Global Decision Support System (GDSS2), Theater Situation Reports, and aircrew Deployed Status Reports (DSR).  Aircraft equipped with Blue Force Tracker (BFT) devices  are  tracked  near  real  time  via  the  Common  Operating  Picture  (COP).    Inputs  to  these various tracking tools are provided by the C2 agency with OPCON.  (T-2) 2.5.1.  PIC or mission commander flight reporting duties:  (T-3) 2.5.1.1.  Stations With MAF C2 Agency.  Aircrews will provide a  “Thirty Minute” Out Call.    Transmit  a  UHF  or  VHF  arrival  advisory  to  the  destination  C2  agency approximately  30  minutes  prior  to  arrival.    Provide  Estimated  Time  in  Blocks  (ETB).  Local MAF C2 agents will enter mission data (arrival, departure, and advisory messages) in  GDSS2  when  applicable.    Additionally,  aircrews  must  keep  their  controlling  C2 agency  appraised  of  all  actual  takeoff  and  landing  times,  projected  takeoff  times,  and other related information within 30 minutes after landing.  (T-3)   16  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 2.5.1.2.  Stations  Without  MAF  C2  Agency.    Transmit  mission  data  (arrival,  departure, and advisory messages) to the controlling C2 agency, within 30 minutes after landing, by any  means  available.    (Preference  in  the  following  order:    Defense  Switched  Network (DSN)/  commercial  telephone,  high  frequency  (HF)  phone  patch,  Iridium  Phone).    For critical C2 communications (i.e., aircraft waiver request, maintenance delay, etc.), voice communications are the primary method.  (T-3) 2.5.1.3.  Provide controlling C2 agency with daily DSR.  (T-3) 2.5.1.4.  Reporting Agencies.  See Table 2.1. Table 2.1.  Reporting Agencies. Designation  of  a  COMAFSOF.  IAW  AFI  51-604,  Appointment  to  and  Assumption  of Command and AFI 10-410, Operations Planning: Presentation of Air Force Special Operations Forces, the COMAFSOF is  appointed by COMAFSOC through G-Series orders specifying the individual by name and the geographic area of authority. 2.7.  Mission  Commander    (MC).  A  mission  commander  will  be  designated  when  more  than one  aircraft  or  crew  is  deployed  away  from  home  station  for  training,  exercises,  or  other operations.    The  mission  commander  will  be  rated,  and  should  be  a  field  grade  officer.    The mission or air mission commander (AMC) will not be a primary crew member for exercises, but may fly as a crew member on non-exercise related missions.  Mission commander duties include, but are not limited to (T-2): 2.7.1.  Briefing crews on local operating procedures. 2.7.2.  Coordinating with Air Traffic Control (ATC), Combat Control Team (CCT), Special Tactics  Squadron  (STS),  range  control,  users,  and  others  that  may  have  an  impact  on  the mission. 2.7.3.  Ensuring  personnel  have  ample  and  adequate  billeting,  eating,  and  transportation arrangements. 2.7.4.  Ensuring maintenance personnel know of aircraft and fuel requirements. 2.7.5.  Submitting timely reports on aircraft movements. 2.7.6.  Ensuring  security  of  aircraft  and  personnel  meets  the  requirements  of  AFI  31-101, Integrated Defense (FOUO). 2.8.  Pilot  in  Command  Responsibilities  and  Authority.  AF  Form  4327A  Crew  Flight Authorization (FA) designates a Pilot in Command for all flights.  PIC are (T-2): 2.8.1.  In command of all persons on board the aircraft. 2.8.2.  Responsible  for  the  welfare  of  their  aircrew  members,  Mission  Essential  Personnel (MEP), and the safe accomplishment of the mission. 2.8.3.  Vested  with  the  authority  necessary  to  manage  their  crew  and  safely  accomplish  the mission. AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   19  2.8.4.  The  final  mission  authority  and  will  make  decisions  not  specifically  assigned  to  a higher authority. 2.8.5.  The final authority for accepting a waiver affecting the crew or mission. 2.8.6.  Charged  with  keeping  the  applicable  commander  informed  of  mission  progress  and difficulties. 2.8.7.  The PIC will coordinate with local maintenance for available support, and then report to  AFSOC  Combat  Logistics  Readiness  Center  (LRC):    DSN  579-8925, (850)-884-8925  or 1800451-7705.  When reporting, describe the problem, the assistance available (if any) and assistance required.  Any time the aircraft experiences over a 2-hour maintenance delay the PIC will report to AFSOC LRC as soon as practical (regardless of the support being received from the deployed location). 2.9.  Airborne  Mission  Commander  (AMC).  The  individual  responsible  for  the  overall employment  of  all  air  assets  assigned  to  the  mission.    Required  for  multi-element,  multi-event formations,  and/or  where  mission  complexity  dictates.    The  AMC  will  not  be  a  primary  crew member and should be on headset.  (T-2) 2.10.  Deputy  Mission  Commander  (DMC).  Required on all missions employing a dedicated AMC,  on  all  multi-element  formation  missions,  and  on  all  single-element  formations  of  three aircraft or more.  The DMC assumes command if conditions prevent the AMC from controlling the  mission.    The  DMC  may  be  a  primary  crew  member,  and  is  usually  the  Formation Commander  on  AMC  controlled  missions.    The  DMC  will  not  be  on  the  same  aircraft  as  the AMC.  (T-2) 2.11.  Mission  Clearance  Decision.  The final  decision to  delay a mission may be made either by the agency with OPCON or the PIC when, in the opinion of either, conditions are not safe to start or continue a mission.  Final responsibility for the safe conduct of the mission rests with the PIC.  If the PIC refuses a mission, it will not depart until the conditions have been corrected or improved so that the mission can operate safely.  Another PIC and aircrew will not be alerted to take the same mission under the same conditions.  (T-2) 2.11.1.  Divert  or  Reroute  Authorizations.    Diverting  or  rerouting  a  mission  must  be authorized  by  the  commander  with  OPCON,  except  in  an  emergency  or  when  required  by enroute or terminal weather conditions or facilities.  In the event of an emergency or weather related divert or reroute, the PIC must notify the controlling authority as soon as possible. 2.11.1.1.  The  controlling  agency  directing  the  diversion  or  rerouting  is  responsible  for ensuring destination requirements or facilities are adequate for the aircraft and aircrew. 2.11.1.2.  The PIC will notify the controlling agency of any aircraft or aircrew limitations that may preclude diverting or rerouting the mission. 2.11.2.  When directing an aircraft to an alternate airfield, the controlling agency will ensure the PIC is provided existing and forecasted weather for the alternate.  If the planned alternate is unsuitable upon arrival at destination, the controlling agency will advise the PIC of other suitable alternates. 2.12.  Civilian  Law  Enforcement  Support.  It  is  the  policy  of  the  Department  of  Defense  to cooperate  with  civilian  law  enforcement  officials  to  the  maximum  extent  practicable.    AFI 10801, Defense Support of Civil Authorities (DSCA), incorporates the appropriate directive and   20  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 provides uniform policies and procedures service members must follow when supporting federal, state,  and  local  civilian  law  enforcement  agencies.    It  establishes  specific  limitations  and restrictions on the use of Air Force personnel, equipment, facilities, and services by civilian law enforcement  organizations.    Report  all  requests  for  assistance  and  coordinate  all  requests  from civilian law enforcement authorities through the appropriate C2 channels. AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   21  Chapter 3 AIRCREW COMPLEMENT AND MANAGEMENT 3.1.  Aircrew Qualification.  Each person assigned as a primary crew member must be qualified or in training for qualification in that crew position, mission and Mission Design Series (MDS) aircraft.  This chapter contains Tier 2 requirements in the aircrew qualification, interfly, intrafly and alert duty sections. (T-2)  Tier 3 in the crew complement section.  (T-3) 3.1.1.  Basic  aircraft  qualification  (F  coded)  crew  members  (i.e.,  FP  and  FL)  may  perform primary  crew  duties  on  any  non-contingency  sortie  (including  unilateral  training,  joint training and exercises) when receiving mission qualification training or evaluations, and only while  under  the  supervision  of  a  qualified  instructor  or  flight  examiner  in  their  respective crew position. 3.1.2.  Basic mission capable (M coded) crew members (i.e., MP, MW, MK, and ML) may perform primary crew duties on any unilateral training mission.  For other missions, the unit commander  must  determine  the  readiness  of  each  basic  mission  capable  crew  member  to perform primary crew duties for specific mission tasking. 3.1.3.  Non-current or unqualified (U coded) pilots (i.e., UP) may perform crew duties only on designated training or evaluation missions under the supervision of a qualified instructor or flight examiner pilot. 3.1.4.  Other  non-current  or  U-coded  crew  members  (i.e.,  UP,  UW,  UL,  and  UK)  may perform duties in their primary crew position on any sortie when under direct supervision of a  qualified  instructor  or  flight  examiner  in  their  respective  crew  position.    In  this  case,  the student  crew  member  and  the  instructor  or  flight  examiner  fulfills  the  requirement  for  one primary  position  as  specified  in  Table  3.1  with  the  exception  of  UK.    In  this  case,  one instructor or flight examiner may supervise more than one UK. 3.1.5.  Senior  staff  pilots  or  O-coded  pilots  (OP)  who  have  completed  a  Senior  Staff Familiarization course will occupy the left pilot seat only and be under direct Instructor Pilot (IP) supervision.  These individuals will log OP  for Flight  Authorization Duty Code on the Air  Force  Technical  Order  (AFTO)  Form  781,  ARMS  Aircrew/Mission  Flight  Data Document.  Refer to Paragraph 9.12 for additional restrictions. 3.1.6.  A Weapon Systems Officer (WSO) is an Electronic Warfare Officer (EWO) qualified crew  member.    A  WSO  may  be  qualified  as  either  an  air-land  Combat  Systems  Officer (CSO) and Mission Crew Commander (MCC) or a tactical airdrop CSO.  A CSO or WSO is required per Table 3.1.  A tactical airdrop qualified WSO or CSO is required for all airdrop and low level operations. 3.2.  EC-130J  (Super  J)  Crew  Complement.  The  EC-130J  (Super  J)  crew  complement  is specified in Table 3.1.  Unit commanders may authorize reduced crew complements as noted in the  table.    The  waiver  authority  for  any  additional  crew  complement  reductions,  down  to  the minimum  crew  complement  specified  in  the  aircraft  flight  manual,  is  the  group  commander  or COMAFSOF.  (T-3) 3.2.1.  Augmented crews are required for missions planned to take longer than a basic Flight Duty  Period  (FDP).    Augmenting  aircrew  members  must  be  current,  qualified,  and  mission   22  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 capable  IAW  AFI  11-2EC-130J,  Vol  1,  EC-130J  Aircrew  Training.    In  those  situations requiring augmentation, the crew must be augmented from the start of the duty period. 3.2.2.  With  the  exception  of  the  Combat  Mission  Sortie  (CMS),  all  events  accomplished with a reduced crew complement can be logged as long as the applicable event criteria in AFI 112EC130, Vol 1, are met. Additional  Crew  members  (ACM).  See  AFI  11-401,  Aviation  Management,  MAJCOM Supplement. 3.4.  Interfly.  Interfly  is  the  exchange  and/or  substitution  of  aircrew  members  and/or  aircraft between  MAJCOMs  to  accomplish  flying  missions.    Normally,  interfly  should  be  limited  to specific  operations/tests,  exercises,  or  special  circumstances.    Reference  AFI  11-401,  Aviation Management, and MAJCOM Supplement.  (T-2) 3.4.1.  HQ  AFSOC/A4RX  and  National  Guard  Bureau  (NGB)/A4MY  maintains  current Memorandum  of  Agreements  (MOA)  between  AFSOC,  AFRC,  ANG,  Air  Force  Material Command (AFMC), Air Education Training Command (AETC), and Air Combat Command (ACC) for interfly using AFSOC assigned aircraft.  Unless specified in the MOA: 3.4.1.1.  Aircraft ownership will not be transferred. 3.4.1.2.  The operational squadron will prepare and sign the flight authorizations.   24  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 3.4.1.3.  As a minimum,  crew member(s) will be  Basic  Aircraft Qualified  (BAQ) in  the MDS aircraft and model, as well as systems or configuration required to  fly the aircraft and/or mission. 3.4.1.4.  Aircrew will follow operational procedures defined in AFI 11-2EC-130J, Vol 3, EC130J  Operations  Procedures,  AFTTP  3-1.E/MC-130J,  Tactical  Employment  E/MC-130J  (Classified)  and  33.E/MC-130J,  Combat  Aircraft  Fundamentals  E/MC-130J,  and the applicable Technical Order (s) (TO) for the MDS. 3.4.1.5.  A  flight  and  ground  mishap  reporting  responsibility  will  be  handled  IAW  AFI 91-204, Safety Investigations and Reports. 3.4.2.  Waiver Authority. 3.4.2.1.  With a valid MOA IAW AFI 11-401, group commander or COMAFSOF is the approval authority for interfly on AFSOC aircraft under their control. 3.4.2.2.  No  MOA/Expired  MOA.    The  interfly  of  aircrew  members  from  different MAJCOMs or the interfly of active duty and ANG aircrews require approval from each MAJCOM/A3 and the NGB/A3, as applicable. 3.4.2.3.  Contingency  operations  must  be  approved  by  HQ  AFSOC/A3,  the  respective MAJCOM/A3, and NGB/A3. 3.4.3.  Aircrew members assigned to the USAF Weapons School (USAFWS) are authorized to participate in orientation flights in AFSOC aircraft operated by crews from 14th Weapons Squadron (WPS). 3.4.4.  Aircrew  members  assigned  to  the  USAFWS  are  authorized  to  occupy  duty  positions on  AFSOC  aircraft  operated  by  14  WPS.    Crew  members  must  be  under  instructor supervision if not current and qualified in the MDS. 3.4.4.1.  The  above  authorizations  are  extended  to  senior  leadership  in  the  USAFWS chain of command. 3.4.4.2.  Flights conducted under the above provisions will be within the normal syllabi. 3.5.  Intrafly.  Intrafly  is  the  exchange  and/or  substitution  of  aircrew  members  from  separate units  under  the  same  MAJCOM  to  accomplish  flying  missions.    Normally,  intrafly  should  be used only to relieve qualified manpower shortfalls.  (T-2) 3.5.1.  The Group Commander possessing the aircraft or COMAFSOF is approval authority for intrafly between units. 3.5.2.  As  a  minimum,  crews  will  be  qualified  in  the  MDS-aircraft  and  model,  as  well  as systems or configuration required to fly the aircraft and/or mission. 3.5.3.  Aircrew  will  follow  operational  procedures  defined  in  AFI  11-2EC-130J,  Vol  3, AFTTP  31.E/MC-130J  and  AFTTP  3-3.E/MC-130J,  and  the  applicable  TO  for  the  MDS.  EC-130J aircrews flying C130J aircraft will follow AFI 11-2EC-130J, Vol 1, Vol 2, EC-130J Evaluation Criteria and the applicable TO for the MDS. 3.6.  Orientation  Flights  and  Incentive  Flights.  Refer to DoD 4515.13-R, Air Transportation Eligibility, AFI 11-401, Aviation Management, and the appropriate MAJCOM supplement. AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   25  3.7.  Alert Duty.  Alert personnel are those required to be on duty for the prompt execution of a mission.    Alert  crews  will  be  readily  available  in  a  location  that  allows  the  crew  to  meet  the required  time  to  launch  from  notification.    Suitable  facilities  include  adequate  sleeping accommodations for the entire crew.  Publish flight authorizations for the alert crew to cover the entire alert tour.  See AFI 11-202, Vol 3, General Flight Rules, and MAJCOM Supplement for alert procedures.  (T-2) 3.8.  Flight Duty Period and Crew Rest Restrictions.  See AFI 11-202, Vol 3, General Flight Rules, and MAJCOM Supplement. 3.8.1.  Crew  Chiefs/MEP.    The  crew  chief  is  responsible  to  the  Aircraft  Commander.    The aircraft  commander  will  determine  how  long  the  Crew  Chief  /MEP  can  safely  perform aircraft recovery actions.  The Crew Chief/MEP must have the opportunity to sleep 8 hours uninterrupted  within  each  24  hour  period,  reference  AFI  21-101,  Aircraft  and  Equipment Maintenance Management Policy for additional guidance. 3.9.  Counter-Fatigue  Management  Program.  See AFI 11-202, Vol 3,  General  Flight Rules, and MAJCOM Supplement.   26  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 Chapter 4 AIRCRAFT OPERATING GUIDLELINES AND RESTRICTIONS 4.1.  Objective.  The  objective  of  the  aircraft  maintenance  team  is  to  provide  an  aircraft  for launch with all equipment operational Fully Mission Capable (FMC).  However, under specific circumstances,  some  missions  can  be  safely  operated  without  all  equipment  being  operational.  The  final  responsibility  regarding  equipment  required  for  a  mission  rests  with  the  PIC.    If  one crew accepts an aircraft to operate a mission or mission segment without an item or system, this acceptance does not commit that crew, or a different crew, to accept subsequent operations with the  same  item  or  system  inoperative.    When  the  PIC  considers  an  item  essential,  designate  the component  Mission  Essential  (ME)  on  the  AFTO  Form  781A,  Maintenance  Discrepancy  and Work  Document,  and  the  item  will  be  repaired  or  replaced  prior  to  departure.    This  chapter contains Tier 2 requirements in sections relating to MEL, waiver protocol, landing gear system, and soft panel operations.  Tables 4.3 Communications, 4.5 Equipment, 4.6 Fire Protection, 4.7 Flight Controls, 4.11 Indicating/Recording System,  4.13 Lights, 4.14 Navigation, 4.15 Oxygen, 4.17 System Integration and Display, and 4.19 Doors contain Tier 2 requirements as well.  Tier 3 requirements are contained in the one-time flight section as well as Table 4.21 Powerplant. 4.2.  Policy.  This chapter provides guidance on how to operate with degraded equipment.  If the PIC  elects  to  operate  with  degraded  equipment  or  aircraft  system(s),  coordinate  mission requirements  (i.e.,  revised  departure  times,  fuel  requirements,  maintenance  requirements,  etc.), prior to flight with the mission control agency to ensure the decision does not adversely impact follow-on missions. 4.3.  Minimum  Equipment  List  (MEL)  Policy.  The MEL is  a pre-launch document that lists the  minimum  equipment/systems  to  operate  the  aircraft  prior  to  takeoff.    It  is  impractical  to prepare  a  list  that  would  anticipate  all  possible  combinations  of  equipment  malfunctions  and contingent  circumstances.  Consider equipment/systems with  no listed  exceptions as  grounding items.  (T-2) 4.3.1.  The  PIC  shall  account  for  the  possibility  of  additional  failures  during  continued operation with inoperative systems or components.  The MEL is not intended for continued operation over an indefinite period with systems/subsystems inoperative. 4.3.2.  All  emergency  equipment  will  be  installed  unless  specifically  exempted  by  mission requirements/directives. 4.3.3.  PIC  operating  with  waiver(s)  for  degraded  equipment  shall  coordinate  mission requirements (revised departure times, fuel requirements, and maintenance requirements). 4.3.4.  If beyond C2 communication capability, or when it is necessary to protect the crew or aircraft from a situation not covered by this chapter and immediate action is required, the PIC may deviate.  Report deviations (without waiver) to OG/CC within 48 hours, if requested. 4.4.  Waiver  Protocol.  Waivers to operate with  degraded equipment are granted on a case-by-case basis.  (T-2) 4.4.1.  MAJCOM/A3  is  the  MEL  waiver  authority  for  mission  continuation.    Initiate  the request with MAJCOM C2 agency. AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   27  4.4.1.1.  While on ANG directed missions, NGB/A3 delegates MEL  waiver authority to the Unit OG/CC (or equivalent). 4.4.2.  The waiver request will include: 4.4.2.1.  Reason for the request. 4.4.2.2.  Individual crew member qualifications. 4.4.2.3.  Mission leg(s) requiring the waiver. 4.5.  Technical Assistance Service.  The PIC may request (at any time in the decision process) technical  support  and  additional  assistance  from  their  home  unit,  MAJCOM  staff,  and maintenance representatives. 4.6.  One-Time  Flights.  An aircraft may be released for a one-time flight with a condition that might be hazardous for continued use, provided the aircraft is airworthy for one flight to a repair station.    Refer  to  TO  00-20-1,  Aerospace  Equipment  Maintenance  Inspection,  Documentation, Policies, and Procedures, for downgrade authority and procedures. 4.6.1.  One-time  flight  approval  authority  is  OG/CC  or  equivalent-level  commander  with OPCON  for  MEL  listed  items.    The  193  SOW  Maintenance  Group  (MXG)/CC  (or designated official), the  senior maintenance officer, or the on-site chief of an AFMC repair team must first authorize the release.  The PIC concurrence is required before the aircraft can be flown.  (T-3) 4.6.1.1.  Any  One-time  flight  request  not  listed  in  the  MEL  additionally  requires MAJCOM/A3 approval.  (T-2) 4.7.  Fuel  System.  The  primary  concern  with  inoperative  fuel  boost  pumps  or  quantity indicators is fuel balance and wing loading.  Degraded operation is permissible, however, flight crews  must  consider  potentially  trapped  fuel  and  decreased  range  should  further  degradation occur.    The  MEL,  included  in  Table  4.8  along  with  the  following  paragraphs,  provides guidelines for degraded fuel system operations under most circumstances. 4.7.1.  In-flight, fuel will not be transferred into or out of a main fuel tank with an inoperative indicator or its symmetrical tank except the following: 4.7.1.1.  Fuel transfer into a main tank with an inoperative indicator may be accomplished during  contingency  or  emergency  fuel  need  situations.    All  transfers,  under  these conditions, require more than one crew member to monitor and coordinate the transfer. 4.7.1.2.  A reliable source of known quantity transferred must be available.  This source can be either the internal aircraft operating fuel quantity indicators or in-flight refueling tanker fuel on load data. 4.7.1.2.1.  Begin  crossfeed  operation  when  the  symmetrically  opposite  quantity indicator has decreased to 1,500 pounds (inboards) and 2,500 pounds (outboards). 4.7.1.3.  Engine  out  training  using  the  engine  corresponding  to  the  inoperative  indicator or its symmetrically opposite will not be conducted during tank to engine operation. 4.7.1.4.  Maintain symmetrical engine fuel flow. 4.7.1.5.  Plan to land with a minimum of 6,000 pounds calculated main tank fuel.   28  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 4.7.1.6.  When  an  external  tank  indicator  is  inoperative  and  the  tank  cannot  be  visually checked empty due to foam modification, comply with the following prior to flight: 4.7.1.6.1.  Check  pressure  with  each  pump  in  the  external  tank.    If  no  pressure  is obtained, the tank is verified empty. 4.7.1.6.2.  If  pressure  is  obtained,  ground  transfer  the  fuel  from  the  external  tank.  Defuel the external tank if unable to ground transfer. 4.7.1.6.3.  When unable to verify an external tank is empty prior to engine start, place the tank on cross-feed until no pressure is obtained.  This will be completed prior to takeoff. 4.7.1.6.4.  Maintain  symmetrical  tanks  within  1,000  pounds  at  all  times.    If  small amounts (4,000 pounds or less) must be transferred, then transfer up to 1,000 pounds into  the  tank  with  the  inoperative  indicator  followed  by  an  equal  amount  into  the tank(s) with operative indicator(s).  If large amounts of fuel must be transferred, then transfer  1,000  pounds  into  the  tank  with  the  inoperative  indicator,  then  up  to  2,000 pounds  as  needed  into  the  tank(s)  with  the  operative  indicators,  then  up  to  1,000 pounds  as  needed  into  the  tank  with  the  inoperative  indicator  to  bring  all  tanks symmetrical,  or  continue  up  to  2,000  pounds  as  needed,  repeating  the  cycle  until desired fuel quantity and balance is achieved in applicable tanks. 4.8.  Landing  Gear  System.  If  a  landing  gear  system  or  position  indicator  malfunction  is encountered, only a full  stop  landing will be made.  The discrepancy  will be corrected prior to the  next  flight.    Exception:    If  repair  capability  does  not  exist  and  a  positive  determination  is made that further flight can be accomplished with the gear down and locked, the aircraft may be flown  to  a  destination  where  repair  capability  exists  provided  the  gear  is  not  moved  from  the down and locked position.  Required en route stops are authorized.  (T-2) 4.9.  Navigation  Systems.  Refer  to  the  navigation  systems  performance  requirements  as outlined  in  Table  4.14,  Chapter  11  of  this  instruction,  and  applicable  sections  of  the  Flight Information Planning document for the route structures and intended areas of operation. 4.10.  Soft Panel Operations. 4.10.1.  For  partial  or  complete  hard  panel  failures,  aircrews  may  revert  to  soft  panel operations.  Normally, if a soft panel is selected due to hard panel failure, it should be used for the remainder of the flight.  Doing so will mitigate the hazards associated with restoring hard  panel  functionality  for  an  item  when  the  mission  computer  commanded-state  is unknown. the  ENGINE  SHUTDOWN  and  BEFORE  LEAVING AIRPLANE checklists after the aircraft is parked will ensure the soft panel retains control of the  particular  item  throughout  shutdown.    In  all  cases,  PIC  must  consider  the  increased workload associated with using soft panels.   Accomplishing 4.10.2.  Hard panel failures may be the result of a physical failure or loss of communication with the mission computer (MC), an aircraft reboot may recover hard panel functionality.  To determine  if  hard  panel  functionality  can  be  regained,  the  following  procedures  must  be followed in sequential order: 4.10.2.1.  Completely  power  down  when  accomplishing  the  BEFORE  LEAVING AIRPLANE checklist. AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   29  4.10.2.2.  Complete all checklist items in the POWER UP checklist.  Do not proceed past the  POWER  UP  checklist  until  it  can  be  determined  if  the  hard  panel  has  recovered.  Depending  on  the  system  effected  (such  as  APU,  bleed  air,  landing  gear,  etc.),  do  not apply bleed air or hydraulics until hard panel functionality can be determined. 4.10.2.3.  To  determine  if  a  hard  panel  has  recovered,  ensure  hard  panel  and  soft  panel selections/settings are identical.   Press  the Line Select  Key (LSK) to  turn the soft panel OFF.  If a Communication/Navigation/Identification (CNI) “Check (CHK) HARD PNL” or  a  referenced  hard  panel  fault  Advisory  Caution  and  Warning  System  (ACAWS) message  (i.e.,  “APU  PNL  FAULT”,  “DEF  SYS  PNL  FAULT”,  etc.)  does  not  appear, press the “VERIFY OFF LSK”.  If feasible, check hard panel functionality. 4.10.2.4.  If  a  CNI  “CHK  HARD  PNL”  or  a  referenced  hard  panel  fault  ACAWS message  appears,  the  hard  panel  has  not  recovered.    The  “CHK  HARD  PNL”  message indicates there is a mismatch between the soft panel and hard panel commands to the MC independent  of  physical  switch  positions.    Referenced  hard  panel  fault  messages  are selfexplanatory. 4.10.2.5.  If it is determined that the hard panel has not recovered, at the PIC‘s discretion, the  mission  may  continue  to  a  station  supporting  a  repair  capability,  including  en  route stops.  Do not reselect the hard panel.  If a flight must continue under the control of two or more soft panels, a waiver is required.  (T-2) 4.10.3.  After  returning  to  home  station  or  repair  facility  with  a  hard  panel  malfunction, aircrews  will  shut  down  and  turn  the  aircraft  over  to  logistics  personnel  for  required maintenance  actions.    Annotate  that  soft  panel  operation  is  selected  in  the  aircraft maintenance forms with a thorough description of the equipment failure/discrepancy.  (T-2) 4.11.  MEL Table Definitions/Column Identifiers. 4.11.1.  Installed – Number of components or systems installed. 4.11.1.1.  In some cases, a component can be controlled from either a hard panel or from a soft panel.  Similarly, some indications can be viewed  on either a hard panel or a soft panel.    Since  switch  functions  (or  indications)  may  be  duplicated  on  each  of  the  three Communication/Navigation/Identification  Management  Unit  (CNI-MU)  displays,  the number  of  switches  (or  indications)  installed  may  not  always  be  clear.    To  clarify  this condition,  switches  (or  indications)  are  listed  as  ‘1’  in  the  installed  column  even  when they are duplicated on a soft panel. 4.11.1.2.  Although the indications on each pilot’s Heads Down Displays (HDD) can be repeated  on  more  than  one  HDD,  repetitions  of  data  in  excess  of  one  per  pilot  are  not relevant  for  flight  and  are  not  counted  in  this  MEL.    In  general,  the  flight  deck  is designed  to  provide  one  set  of  data  for  the  pilot  and  one  set  of  data  for  the  copilot  (in addition  to  the  standby  instruments).    Thus,  for  most  HDD  indications,  the  number installed is listed as ‘2’ one for each pilot. 4.11.2.  Required – The minimum number (quantity) of items required for operation provided the conditions specified in the remarks or exception column are met. 4.11.2.1.  Unless  otherwise  noted,  when  the  item  is  a  switch  (or  indication)  which  is duplicated on a soft panel, the number required for dispatch may be satisfied by either the   30  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 hard  panel  switch  (or  indication)  or  by  the  switch  (indication)  on  one  of  the  associated soft panels.  For HDD indications, the number required is ‘2’ if both pilots must have an indication, ‘1’ if only one pilot must have an indication and ‘0’ if neither pilot is required to have the indication.  For essential flight data (heading, altitude, airspeed, attitude and when required, navigation data), the pilot‘s and copilot‘s displays must have independent sources. 4.11.3.  Remarks and Exceptions.  Some technical information and procedures are contained in this column.  This is not all-inclusive; crew members shall refer to the flight manual and other directives for procedures, techniques, limitations, etc.  Note:  Common sense and good judgment  must  be  used  by  all  when  determining  minimum  equipment  requirements,  to preclude  adverse  operational  impact  or  excessive  maintenance  support  requirements.    In those instances where lack of replacement parts or qualified personnel would cause a mission delay,  the  aircraft  may  continue  operations  as  described  in  the  MEL.    Note:    For  certain failures  in  this  section,  a  “^”  following  a  system  item  indicates  that  there  may  be  Special Mission Equipment (SME) remarks or exceptions pertaining to that item in Attachment 5 of this regulation.  The MCC will advise the PIC about the impact that the SME failures have upon specific mission accomplishment.  The PIC will decide whether to have the inoperative SME repaired or perform the mission without the inoperative equipment. Table 4.1.  Air Conditioning and Pressurization. See  AFI  11-301,  Vol  1,  Aircrew  Flight  Equipment  (AFE)  Program,  for minimum aircrew clothing requirements.  All crew members will have nomex gloves in their possession.  When the Foreign Clearance Guide (FCG) requires civilian attire, dress conservatively. 5.1.1.2.  It  is  recommended  that  primary  crew  members  wear  nomex  gloves  during engine start, takeoff, landing, and combat operations. 5.1.1.3.  Crew members will remove rings before performing aircrew duties.  (T-3) 5.1.2.  Personal Requirements. 5.1.2.1.  Passport.  Crew members possessing a valid military passport will carry it on all active  duty  missions.    Exception:    Unit  commanders  may  authorize  newly  assigned personnel who have applied for, but not yet received, a passport to act as crew members on missions not scheduled to transit locations where passports are required.  (T-3) 5.1.2.2.  Shot  Record. requirements for the mission.  (T-3)   Aircrew  members  will  ensure  they  meet  immunization 5.1.2.3.  Driver’s  License.    A  valid  state  and  government  issued  driver's  license  is required  on  each  TDY  where  use  of  US  government  general  purpose  vehicles  may  be required.    Crew  members  will  contact  the  local  airfield  manager  before  driving  on  the flight line.  (T-3) 5.1.2.4.  Identification Tags.  Crew members will wear two identification tags around the neck or carry them in a flight suit pocket on all flights.  (T-3) 5.1.2.5.  Restricted Area Badges.  Carry the restricted area badge on all missions (except actual combat missions).  Display the badge only in designated restricted areas.  (T-3) 5.1.2.6.  Tool  and  Airdrop  Kits.    A  tool  kit  will  be  on  board  the  aircraft  for  all  flights.  One  loadmaster  airdrop  kit  will  also  be  aboard  the  aircraft  for  aerial  delivery  missions.  Units will identify tool kit contents and inventory.  (T-3) 5.1.2.7.  Hostile  Environment  Repair  Kit. (AFSOCM) 11201, Hostile Environmental Repair Procedures.   Refer  to  AFSOC  Command  Manual 5.1.2.8.  Carry  a  headset,  helmet  and  oxygen  mask,  and  operable  night  vision  googles (NVG) compatible flashlight on all flights.  A reflective belt or suitable substitute will be worn  on  flight  lines  during  hours  of  darkness  or  periods  of  reduced  visibility.    Aircrew will ensure that all professional equipment is removed from the aircraft after the mission is  complete.    If  an  item  is  lost,  an  AFTO  Form  781,  Aerospace  Vehicle  Flight  Data Record, entry will be documented.  (T3) AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   63  5.1.2.9.  Crew  members  will  not  wear  wigs,  hairpieces,  rings,  ornaments,  or  earrings  in the aircraft or on the flight line.  Exception:  Crew members may wear plain elastic hair fasteners and/or pins, clips, or barrettes providing they do not interfere with the wearing of headsets, or the donning of oxygen equipment.  They will be accounted for before and after flight.  (T-3) 5.1.3.  Aircrew Publications Requirements. 5.1.3.1.  PIC will ensure the publications specified in Table 5.1 are current and available on the aircraft for all missions.  Each individual aircrew member will ensure they have a current  crew  position  checklist  as  required  in  Table  5.1.    Units  may  specify  additional publications  in  their  local  supplement.    The  use  of  electronic  flight  manuals  in  flight  is authorized  upon  issue.    Primary  crew  members  should  carry  their  respective  crew position aircrew guide (ACG) on all missions.  (T-3) Table 5.1.  Aircrew Publications. Publication Pilot/Combat Systems Operator Flight Crew Checklist Aircrew Pilot/Combat Systems Operator Loadmasters Flight Crew Checklist Loadmaster Mission Crew Commander Flight Crew Checklist Mission Crew Commander Electronic Communications Systems (ECS) Operator Flight Crew Checklist Electronic Communications Systems Operator AFI 11-202, Vol 3, General Flight Rules, w/AFSOC supplement AFI 11-2EC-130J, Vol 3, EC-130J Operating Procedures On Aircraft On Aircraft TO 1C-130J-1, Flight Manual On Aircraft TO 1C-130J-1-1, Flight Manual Performance Data TO 1C-130J-1-4, Communications/Navigation/Identification-Management System (CNI-MS) Operator Manual ATP-56(B), NATO Air-to-Air Refueling Procedures AFTTP 3-3.E/MC-130J Combat Aircraft Fundamentals E/MC-130J On Aircraft On Aircraft On Aircraft On Aircraft AFI 13-217, Drop Zone and Landing Zone Operations On Aircraft (Super J)   64  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 Publication AFI 11-231, Computed Air Release Point Procedures Aircrew On Aircraft (Super J) (airdrop qualified only) TO 1C-130J-9, Cargo Loading Manual On Aircraft (Super J) TO 1C-130J-9CL-1, Cargo Loading Checklist USAF Series C-130J Aircraft Loadmaster TO 1C-130J-5-2, Load Data Manual On Aircraft (Super J) TO 1C-130J-43 (series -2 / -3 / -4 and -5) ECS carry-on kit (mission sorties only) AFSOC Command Manual (AFSOCM) 11-201, Hostile Environment Repair Procedures On Aircraft 5.1.4.  Aircrew Intelligence Briefing.  Aircrews will receive an intelligence briefing that will emphasize  terrorist,  enemy,  and  friendly  political  and  military  development  in  the  area  in which they will be flying.  Obtain timely intelligence updates prior to entering a specific area of  operations  (AOR).    In  theater,  aircrews  should  receive  intelligence  updates  on  initial arrival  at  a  forward  operating  location  (FOL),  or  en  route  stop,  and  thereafter  when significant  developments  occur.    Report  information  of  possible  intelligence  value  to  the local intelligence office as soon as practical to ensure timely dissemination of mission reports (MISREPs).  (T-3) 5.2.  Pre-Departure. 5.2.1.  Flight Crew Information File (FCIF). 5.2.1.1.  Review  Volume  I,  Part  A,  of  the  Flight  Crew  Information  File  (FCIF)  before  all missions.  (T-3) 5.2.1.2.  If material has been added to the FCIF since the last review, enter the latest FCIF item  number,  date,  and  initials  on  the  AF  Form  4121,  FCIF  Currency  Record,  or approved electronic equivalent (Patriot Excalibur (PEX), etc.).  (T-3) 5.2.1.2.1.  Crew  members  delinquent  in  FCIF  and  joining  a  mission  en  route  will receive  an  FCIF  update  from  their  primary  aircrew  member  counterpart  on  that mission.    Instructor  pilots  flying  with  general  officers  are  responsible  for  briefing appropriate FCIF items.  (T-3) 5.2.1.2.2.  Crew  members  that  do  not  have  a  unit  FCIF  card  or  approved  electronic equivalent (not assigned or attached to the unit) will certify FCIF review by entering the last FCIF number and their initials beside their name on the file copy of the flight authorization or the orders.  (T3) 5.2.1.2.3.  OGV  Read  File  (ORF).    Group  Standardization  and  Evaluation  (OGV)  is the  OPR  for  the  OGV  Read  File.    Items  in  OGV  Read  File  may  include  local procedures  and  emphasis  items  (non-safety  of  flight  related).    Crews  will  follow procedures as outlined above in Paragraph 5.2.1.2.2.  (T-3) 5.2.2.  Aircraft  Mission  Kits.    Units  will  maintain  one  mission  kit  per  aircraft.    The  entire mission kit may be stored electronically on an approved e-tools device and must follow the AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   65  guidelines as established in previous paragraphs.  Prior to off-station departures, the PIC or designated representative will ensure a current  mission kit is  on board the aircraft.  The kit will  contain,  but  is  not  limited  to,  the  items  listed  in  Table  5.2.    Current  Operations  will maintain this kit and issue to the crew.  Mission kits will include the following items:  (T-2) Table 5.2.  Aircraft Mission Kit  (T-2). Note:  Units may modify the kit to carry only FLIP documents for the theater in which the mission will operate. 5.2.4.  Flight Plan/Data Verification.  (T-2) 5.2.4.1.  Computer  Flight  Plan(s)  (CFP):    CFP  are  the  official  sources  of  performance, navigation,  and  climatic  data,  including  en  route  wind  information.    If  stand-alone computer  based  plans  are  used,  each  mission  segment  should  utilize  best  wind  data available.  Use only AFSOC validated CFP.   (T-2) 5.2.4.1.1.  Use  CFP  to  the  maximum  extent  practical.    Flight  crews  may  manually compute  flight  plans.    The  PIC  has  final  responsibility  for  flight  plan  accuracy  and diplomatic clearance compliance.  (T-3) 5.2.4.1.2.  Verify  CFP  for  route  of  flight  and  fuel  computation  accuracy  before departure.  All waypoint data retrieved from a database should be verified by one or more of the following methods:  (T-3) 5.2.4.1.2.1.  Latitude/longitude from current FLIP.  (T-3) 5.2.4.1.2.2.  Bearing/distance from a flight plan.  (T-3) 5.2.4.1.2.3.  Ground Based NAVAIDs.  (T-3) AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   67  5.2.4.2.  When conducting Drop Zone (DZ)/Landing Zone (LZ) operations, both pilots or one  pilot  and  CSO  will  verify  CNI-MU  computed  air  release  point  (CARP)/LZ information with a valid DZ/LZ survey.  Refer to AFI 13-217, Drop Zone and Landing Zone Operations, for DZ/LZ survey information/requirements/applicability.  (T-2) 5.2.5.  COMMUNICATIONS SECURITY (COMSEC) and Classified Material.  Obtain and safeguard  current  COMSEC  and  other  classified/keying  material  required  for  the  mission.  Carry  authenticators  and  IFF  Mode  IV  codes,  when  flying  into  an  ADIZ,  participating  in exercises, on overseas missions, deployments, and when specified in operation plans.   (T-2) 5.2.5.1.  The base COMSEC custodian has access to the AFKAG 44/AFKAG 14 and can assist  in  obtaining  the  material  required  for  the  mission.    Squadrons  maintain  the COMSEC material used on most missions.  All squadron members that require access to COMSEC  material  will  be  properly  trained.    Base/squadron  COMSEC  Responsible Officer (CRO) is the point of contact for current training requirements.  (T-2) 5.2.5.2.  Command  and  Control  Center  (CCC)  will  provide  temporary  storage  for COMSEC/classified materials during ground time at en route stops.  Issue and turn-in of COMSEC is normally a function of the squadron CRO.  (T-3) 5.2.5.2.1.  Remove  classified/sensitive  information  (such  as  secure  voice/(high performance  waveform  (HPW),  IFF,  mission  information)  stored  in  all  aircraft systems.   (T-2) 5.2.5.3.  In the event of an emergency, destroy classified material and equipment prior to crash landing or bailout, if possible.   (T-2) 5.2.6.  Briefing  Requirements.    Refer  to  the  appropriate  193d  SOW  briefing  guides  for content.  Crew members will not fly unless they attend the crew briefings for their mission.  Exception:  When pre-mission requirements dictate, PIC may excuse certain crew members from  the  briefing.    The  PIC  will  ensure  that  those  personnel  receive  a  face-to-face  briefing prior to engine start.  (T-3) 5.2.7.  Call  Signs.   Use  the  Voice  Call  Sign  Listing  or  as  specified  in  mission directives/tasking for all missions except local area training missions.  Use squadron or wing static call signs as directed for local area training missions.  (T-3) 5.2.7.1.  Aeromedical  Evacuation.    Preface  normal  call  sign  with  "AIR  EVAC"  when patients are on board.   (T-2) 5.2.7.2.  Search  and  Rescue  (SAR).    When  tasked  to  participate  in  SAR operations,  use the call sign "AIR FORCE RESCUE" plus the last five digits of the aircraft tail number.   (T-2) 5.2.8.  Departure/Arrival Planning.  Comply with AFI 11-202, Vol 3, General Flight Rules, and AFMAN 11-217, Vol 1, Instrument Flight Procedures.  If using a flight plan furnished by another agency, the PIC and CSO will verify routes and flight altitudes to ensure proper terrain clearance.  (T-2) 5.2.9.  Takeoff and Landing Data (TOLD) Verification Requirement.   (T-2) 5.2.9.1.  To verify CNI TOLD, both pilots will cross-check CNI TOLD INIT entries.  (T-3)   68  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 5.2.9.2.  TOLD  ENTRIES  Takeoff  Page  3/4  and  4/4.    For  an  IFR  departure,  aircraft weight must be less than or equal to the calculated maximum aircraft weight for the type of  three-engine  departure  listed  (normal  or  50-flap  at  obstacle  clearance  speed)    Note:  CNI TOLD Takeoff Page 3/4 (Wedge Obstacle) defaults to the minimum 4 and 3 Engine Climb gradients to IAW AFI 11202, Vol 3, General Flight Rules.  (T-2) 5.2.10.  Adverse Weather Procedures.   (T-2) 5.2.10.1.  Flight into areas of forecast or reported severe turbulence is prohibited.  (T-2) 5.2.10.1.1.  Anytime  windshear  may  be  encountered  on  departure  or  approach,  it  is recommended  that  aircrews  select  weather  mode  on  one  NAV  RADAR  display  and windshear mode on another NAV RADAR display.  (T-2) 5.2.10.1.2.  The  PIC  is  responsible  for  ensuring  all  passengers  are  seated,  with  seat belts  fastened,  when  areas  of  moderate  or  greater  turbulence  are  encountered  or anticipated.  (T-3)  WARNING:  Serious injury may occur if passengers do not have their seat belts fastened and the aircraft encounters moderate or severe turbulence. 5.2.10.2.  Flight  into  areas  of  forecast  or  reported  severe  icing  is  prohibited.    Prolonged operation, such as cruise flight or holding, in areas of moderate icing should be avoided.  (T-2) 5.2.10.2.1.  Do not takeoff under conditions of freezing rain or freezing drizzle.  (T-2) 5.2.10.2.2.  Freezing  precipitation,  snow,  freezing  fog  (consider  equivalent  to moderate  icing),  or  temperatures  near  0°  Celsius  (C),  may  cause  ice  or  frost  to accumulate on aircraft surfaces.  When an aircraft requires de-icing/anti-icing prior to takeoff, refer to the following:   (T-2) 5.2.10.2.2.1.  Aircrews  will  only  use  de-ice  and  anti-ice  fluids  listed  in  their respective  flight  manual.    Aircrews  will  be  familiar  with,  and  follow  all restrictions  in  their  associated  flight  manual  with  respect  to  anti-ice/de-ice procedures and holdover times.  (T-3) 5.2.10.2.2.2.  MIL-A-8243 Type I and Type II de-icing fluids do not provide any anti-icing benefit, and therefore do not have holdover times.  (T-3) 5.2.10.2.2.3.  In  all  cases,  PICs  will  ensure  a  visual  inspection  of  the  aircraft  is completed within 5 minutes of departure.  (T-3) 5.2.10.3.  Do  not  fly  directly  above  (within  2,000  feet)  thunderstorms  or  cumulonimbus clouds.    If  unable  to  clear  thunderstorms  or  cumulonimbus  clouds  by  at  least  2000  feet vertically, avoid them by at least: :  (T-2) 5.2.10.3.1.  20 nautical miles (nm) at or above flight level (FL) 230.  (T-3) 5.2.10.3.2.  10 nm below FL 230.  (T-3) 5.2.10.3.3.  5  nm  for  tactical  low-level  operations.    Avoid  gust  fronts  and  winds preceding a rapidly moving thunderstorm.    CAUTION:  Aircraft damage may occur 20 nm or more from any thunderstorms.  Aircrews must familiarize themselves with information on thunderstorm development and hazards.  Refer to AFH 11-203, Vol 1, Weather for Aircrews. AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   69  5.2.10.4.  The  use  of  ground-based  radar  as  a  means  of  thunderstorm  avoidance  should only be used to assist in departing an inadvertently penetrated area of significant weather.  It should never be considered a normal avoidance procedure.  When relying exclusively on  ground-based  radar  for  weather  avoidance,  and  the  ground  controller  is  unable  to provide avoidance instructions, attempt to maintain VMC by:  (T-3) 5.2.10.4.1.  Changing routing.  (T-3) 5.2.10.4.2.  Diverting to alternate.  (T-3) 5.2.10.4.3.  Declaring an emergency and requesting priority assistance.  (T-3) 5.2.10.4.4.  Use  extreme  caution  when  flying  into  an  area  of  known  or  forecast moderate or greater mountain wave turbulence.  (T-3) 5.3.  Pre-Flight. 5.3.1.  Operational  Risk  Management  (ORM).    ORM  is  a  logic  based,  common  sense approach  to  making  calculated  decisions  on  human,  material,  and  environmental  factors before, during, and after all operations.  USAF policy on ORM is contained in AFI 90-802, Risk  Management.    PIC  will  accomplish  ORM  worksheets  IAW  AFSOC/MAJCOM  and local guidance as part of preflight activities.  (T-2) 5.3.1.1.  Flying  units  will  develop  a  local  ORM  program  to  include  personal  ORM  risk assessment for all missions.  (T-3) 5.3.1.2.  The  PIC  will  ensure  an  ORM  risk  assessment  is  accomplished  by  all  crew members as part of pre-flight activities.  (T-3) 5.3.2.  AFTO Forms 781, Aerospace Vehicle Flight Data Record. 5.3.2.1.  Review  AFTO  Form  781  series  before  applying  power  to  the  aircraft  or operating  aircraft  systems.    An  exceptional/conditional  release  must  be  signed  before flight.    A  maintenance  officer,  maintenance  superintendent,  or  authorized  civilian normally  signs  the  exceptional/conditional  release.    If  one  of  these  individuals  is  not available, the PIC may sign the exceptional/conditional release.  When a release is signed by the PIC, it is effective only for those flights in which the releasing PIC participates as an aircrew member.  Ensure the DD Form 1896,  Jet Fuel Identiplate, and AIR card are aboard the aircraft.  (T-3) 5.3.2.2.  One-Time  Flights.    An  aircraft  may  be  released  for  a  one-time  flight  with  a condition that might be hazardous for continued use, provided the aircraft is airworthy for one flight  to  a repair station.  Refer to TO 00-20-1, Aerospace Equipment Maintenance Inspection,  Documentation,  Policies,  and  Procedures,  for  downgrade  authority  and procedures. is  OG/CC  or  equivalent-level 5.3.2.2.1.  One-time  flight  approval  authority commander  with  operational  control  (OPCON)  for  items  listed  in  the  MEL.    (T-3)  Any  one-time  flight  request  not  listed  in  the  MEL  requires  MAJCOM/A3  approval.  (T-2)  The PIC concurrence is required before the aircraft can be flown.  (T-3) 5.3.3.  Authority to Clear a Red X.  Pilots are not normally authorized to clear a Red X.  If a situation is encountered where the aircraft is on a Red X and qualified maintenance personnel are  not  available  to  clear  it,  the  AC  may  obtain  authorization  to  clear  the  Red  X  from  the   70  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 home  station  MXG/CC  or  designated  representative,  in  accordance  with  TO  00-20-1.  Exception:    See  Chapter  10,  Local  Operating  Procedures,  for  additional  guidance  on clearing Red X(s). 5.3.3.1.  At  en  route  stations,  loadmasters  are  authorized  to  clear  Red  X  symbols  for; intake  and  exhaust  inspections,  dust  covers  and  plugs  installed,  and  aircraft  panels removed and installed to facilitate other maintenance. 5.3.4.  Dash  One  Preflight  Inspection  Requirements.    The  aircrew  Dash  One  preflight inspection, once completed, is valid for 72 hours provided the aircraft is sealed. 5.3.4.1.  When  an  aircrew  assumes  a  pre-flighted  spare  or  quick-turn,  a  thorough  visual inspection will be performed, paying particular attention to areas affected by maintenance or servicing.  (T-3) inspection 5.3.4.2.  Except  to  prepare  for  operational  readiness  exercise  (ORE),  operational readiness and contingencies/evacuations,  Dash  One  preflight  inspections  are  normally  done  in preparation  for  flight  by  the  aircrew  assigned  to  fly  the  mission  designated  for  that aircraft, that day. inspection (CUI) (ORI), combined unit 5.3.4.2.1.  The following guidelines apply to aircrew assigned to preflight and/or seal aircraft.  A crew will not preflight more than 4 aircraft in a 12-hour period.  Refer to crew  rest/flight  duty  period  guidance  in  AFI  11-202,  Vol  3,  General  Flight  Rules.  Aircrews performing preflight duties will be afforded 12 hours rest between preflight shifts. 5.3.4.2.2.  Duties  Not  Including  Flying  (DNIF)  current  and  qualified  crew  members may  accomplish  pre-flights  with  the  concurrence  of  the  flight  surgeon.    It  is  the responsibility of the crew member to know his/her duty limitations.  Crew members the  AF  Form  1042,  Medical should  have Recommendations  for  Flying  or  Special  Operations  Duty,  appropriately  IAW  with AFI 48-123, Medical Examinations and Standards. flight  surgeon  document the 5.3.5.  Alert Aircraft Procedures.  Maintain aircraft on alert status as follows:  (T-3) 5.3.5.1.  Park the aircraft in  a designated alert  parking area to  expedite taxi and takeoff.  (T-3) 5.3.5.2.  Aircraft  preflight  times  and  aircraft  preflight  validity  period,  should  follow  the guidance in TO 00-20-1, Aerospace Equipment Maintenance Inspection, Documentation, Policies, and Procedure. 5.3.5.3.  The  alert  aircraft  may  be  flown  for  purposes  other  than  actual  alert  missions provided the following conditions are met: 5.3.5.3.1.  Ensure sufficient fuel remains on board to meet alert commitments. 5.3.5.3.2.  Maintain communications with the primary controlling agency. 5.3.5.3.3.  If  maintenance  actions  are  not  required,  the  aircraft  can  be  resealed  for alert once the thru-flight inspection is completed.  In all cases, a new preflight is not required until the end of the initial preflight period. AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   71  5.3.5.4.  A DD Form 365-4, Weight and Balance Clearance, Form F, will be prepared for the  alert  aircraft.    Alert  crews  are  authorized  to  load  TOLD  using  the  worst  weather conditions expected for the alert period.  Use the TOLD for alert scrambles.  If the alert aircraft is flown for other reasons, use TOLD for the existing weather conditions. 5.3.5.5.  If  the  alert  aircraft  is  changed  to  a  different  pre-flighted/sealed  aircraft,  or  an alert crew change occurs and the same aircraft remains on alert, the preflight or alert crew will,  as  a  minimum,  apply  power  to  the  aircraft  and  check  the  following  systems  (as applicable):  (T-3) 5.3.5.5.1.  AFTO Form 781, Aerospace Vehicle Flight Data Record. 5.3.5.5.2.  Interior and exterior for proper configuration and special equipment.  (T-3) 5.3.5.5.3.  Fuel quantity.  (T-3) 5.3.5.5.4.  Survival and emergency equipment.  (T-3) 5.3.5.5.5.  Navigation and communication equipment.  (T-3) 5.3.5.5.6.  Liquid oxygen quantity.  (T-3) 5.3.5.5.7.  Hydraulic reservoirs and accumulator charges.  (T-3) 5.3.5.5.8.  Publications.  (T-3) 5.3.5.6.  Should  an  aircraft  remain  on  alert  for  more  than  72  hours,  a  complete  aircrew preflight is then required.  (T-3) 5.3.5.7.  Once  the  aircraft  is  accepted  for  alert,  the  loadmaster  will  ensure  an  entry  is made  in  the  AFTO  Form  781H,  Aerospace  Vehicle  Flight  Report  and  Maintenance Document, stating as a minimum, the date and time the aircraft was pre-flighted. 5.3.5.8.  Alert  aircraft  are  off  limits  to  all  personnel  except  alert  crew  members.    No maintenance  may  be  performed  on  the  aircraft  without  the  approval  of  the  unit/mission commander.  Upon receiving orders to launch, the crew is required to check the area in which maintenance was performed prior to flight.  (T-3) 5.3.6.  Aircraft Servicing and Ground Operations. 5.3.6.1.  Aircraft  Refueling.    Fuel  purchases  are  accomplished  IAW  AFI  23-201,  Fuels Management.    Crew  members  may  perform  refueling  duties  at  austere  locations  or  at stations without maintenance support.  Aircrews should not refuel  except in cases when maintenance  support  is  not  readily  available  and  the  mission  would  be  delayed.    Crew members may augment maintenance refueling teams at en route stops.  (T-3) 5.3.6.1.1.  Off  Station  Refueling  Operations.    A  minimum  of  one  aircrew  member must be present during refueling to verify the accuracy of the fuel sale data.  AFMAN 23-110CD,  Air  Force  Supply  Systems  Electronic  Publishing  Library,  requires  the aircrew to obtain the fuel receipt after refueling at a non-Air Force location and verify the accuracy of the date, quantity, type, and tail number.  (T-2) 5.3.6.1.2.  Upon returning to home station the aircrew will pass to maintenance (MX) or the document control officer any and all fuel receipts for the trip.  (T-3)   72  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 5.3.6.1.3.  During  mission  planning,  the  aircrew  will  incorporate  a  refueling  plan  (if required)  by  obtaining  Defense  Energy  Support  Center  (DESC)  Into-Plane  Vendor locations  and  applicable  prices  in  order  to  refuel  at  the  most  economical  locations.  Aircrew  will  use  an  Into-Plane  contract  merchant  when  one  is  reasonably  available.  (T-2) 5.3.6.1.3.1.  A  complete  list  of  Into-Plane  contract  locations  can  be  found  at  the Defense Logistics Agency (DLA) web page;  http://www.airseacard.com/. 5.3.6.2.  Concurrent  Ground  Operations.    Simultaneous  aircraft  refueling/defueling  and cargo  loading  or  maintenance  operations  is  authorized  in  accordance  with  AFI  21-101, Aircraft and Equipment Maintenance Management, TO 00-25-172, Ground Servicing of Aircraft  and  Static  Grounding/Bonding,  MDS  Specific  Technical  Orders,  and  any established local procedures. 5.3.6.3.  Liquid  Oxygen  (LOX)  Servicing.    Under  no  conditions  are  crew  members allowed to service liquid oxygen.  (T-2) 5.3.6.4.  Forward Area Refueling Point Operations.  Refer to AFI 11235, Forward Area Refueling Point (FARP) Operations. 5.3.6.5.  Fire  Protection  and  Crash  Rescue.    See  AFI  13-217,  Drop  Zone  and  Landing Zone Operations, and any AFSOC/MAJCOM specific guidance for specific Fire Fighting and Rescue requirements. 5.3.6.5.1.  The  aircraft  engine  fire  extinguisher  system  fulfills  the  minimum requirements for fire protection during engine start.  If available, position a portable fire extinguisher for added fire protection. 5.3.6.5.2.  A fire guard is required for all engine starts except normal APU starts.  The loadmaster or ground controller may act as fire guard. 5.3.6.6.  Aircrew/Maintenance  Engine  Runs.    Mixed  aircrew/maintenance  engine  runs will  not  normally  be  accomplished.    If  conducted,  review  and  use  the  maintenance  TO procedures.  The cargo door and ramp will be closed for all engine run-up’s above flight idle.  (T-3) 5.3.7.  Aircrew Flight Equipment and Oxygen Requirements. 5.3.7.1.  The  PIC  or  designated  representative  will  ensure  appropriate  serviceable protective  clothing,  aircrew  flight  equipment,  survival  equipment,  and  Dash  21 equipment for the entire mission are available prior to flight and all personnel are briefed or trained in their use prior to departing home station.  (T-3) 5.3.7.1.1.  Prior  to  departing  home  station  and  following  en  route  crew  changes,  the PIC  or  designated  representative  will  review  the  AFTO  Form  46,  Prepositioned Aircrew Flight Equipment, to ensure all required equipment is on board and required inspections  have  been  completed.    The  PIC  or  designated  crew  member  will document and ensure missing aircrew flight equipment is annotated in both the AFTO Form  781,  Aerospace  Vehicle  Flight  Data  Record,  and  AFTO  Form  46, Prepositioned Life Support Equipment. AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015   73  5.3.7.2.  Oxygen.  Oxygen on board for takeoff must be sufficient to accomplish the flight plan route from the ETP, or most distant point to the first suitable airfield.  Minimum for takeoff of no less than 5 liters (Super J).  (T-2)     WARNING:  The passenger oxygen kit (POK) does not protect the wearer from smoke or fumes. 5.3.7.2.1.  All crew members will accomplish a communications and operations check of  their  oxygen  system  prior  to  flight,  which  will  remain  connected  and  readily available.  Walk around bottles do not satisfy this requirement.  (T-3) 5.3.7.2.1.1.  For  primary  crew  members  and  instructors/evaluators  performing duties not  seated in  their primary duty station, utilizing a helmet,  will perform  a communications and oxygen check of the mask and will remain connected to the aircraft oxygen system.  (T-3) 5.3.7.2.1.2.  For the purposes of oxygen requirements, consider Mission Essential Personnel (MEP) as Passengers. 5.3.7.2.2.  Aircrews are authorized to operate aircraft unpressurized above 10,000 ft.  MSL  without  supplemental  oxygen  IAW  AFI  11-202,  Vol  3,  General  Flight  Rules, and AFSOC Supplement. 5.3.7.3.  Life Rafts.  Ensure sufficient wing well life rafts are onboard to accommodate all passengers and aircrew members on overwater flights.  (T-3) 5.3.7.4.  Life  Preserver  Units.    For  overwater  flights,  ensure  a  sufficient  quantity  of  life preservers  are  onboard  for  all  passengers  and  crew  members.    (T-3)    While  overwater, life  preserver  units  (LPU)  will  be  sized  and  readily  available  at  the  crew  member’s station,  and  worn  whenever  below  2,000  feet  overwater  (except  for  takeoff,  approach, and landing).  (T-3)  Crew members wearing a parachute or harness during air refueling overwater  will  also  wear  a  LPU.    (T-3)    For  overwater  missions  carrying  children  and infants,  ensure  the  appropriate  number  and  types  of  LPUs  are  onboard.    (T-3)    Note:  Parachutists’  will  provide  their  own  LPUs.    (T-3)    The  flying  unit  will  ensure  the supported  unit  is  aware  when  route  of  flight  requires  the  use  of  LPUs.    (T-3)    Note:  Infil/Exfil and parachutist operations may preclude immediate issuing of aircraft LPUs to user personnel.  In this case ensure sufficient LPUs are onboard for all personnel. 5.3.7.5.  Anti-exposure  suits.    Anti-exposure  suits  will  be  available  during  overwater flights when route of flight is beyond power off gliding distance from land and the water temperature is 60° Fahrenheit (F) or below.  (T-3)  Exception:  Anti-exposure suits are not  required  when  only  the  approach  or  departure  is  flown  over  water.    If  the  water temperature ranges between 51° F and 60° F, the unit or mission commander may waive or extend the anti-exposure suit requirement after consideration of all risk factors.  (T-3) 5.3.7.6.  Parachutes.    EC-130J  aircraft  will  be  configured  with  one  parachute  for  each crew member.  Units will dictate use of parachutes during combat or acceptance flights.  (T-3) 5.3.7.6.1.  The standard parachutes load for the EC-130J (Slick) is 8. 5.3.7.6.2.  Aircrew  Flight  Equipment  will  verify  the  number  of  crew  members  from Current Operations prior to departing for the aircraft to conduct their Aircrew Flight Equipment preflight.  (T-3)   74  AFI11-2EC-130JV3  8 APRIL 2015 5.3.7.7.  Restraint Harness. 5.3.7.7.1.  Personnel performing duties near an open door in-flight will preflight and wear  a  parachute  or  restraint  harness.    Wear  a  restraint  harness  during  operations below 1,000 feet above ground level (AGL).  Fit the restraint harness and adjust the lifeline  prior  to  takeoff  time.    (T-3)      WARNING:    Position  one  restraint  harness forward  and  aft  of  fight  station  (FS)  245  in  event  the  crew  entrance  door  must  be inspected during flight.  (T-3)  Note:  Connect the hook to a point that will preclude the  wearer  from  exiting  the  aircraft.    (T-3)    Connect  the  lifeline  when  at  or anticipating moving aft of flight station FS 737. 5.3.7.7.2.  The  restraint  harness  lifeline  may  be  attached  to  an  unused,  pre-flighted anchor  cable  that  has  an  anchor  cable  stop  positioned  and  taped  at  FS  737.    Do  not connect the lifeline to an anchor cable that has a parachute static line(s) attached to it for an airdrop. 5.3.7.8.  Survival  Kits/Vests.    All  AFSOC  C-130  aircraft  will  be  configured  with  one survival  kit  (ML-4)  for  each  aircrew  member  for  flights  conducted  beyond  gliding distance of land.
